Topic: Math
Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except
Choices:
  A: (99,10)
  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The first number (x) is a random integer between 0 and 100 inclusive.
  - The second number (y) must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number.
  - If the first number is 1, then the second number must be 1 as well.
  - If the first number is 0, then the second number can be any value less than or equal to 0.

Checking each choice:
  - A: (99,10) satisfies the routine because 10 is less than or equal to the square root of 99.
  - B: (85,9) satisfies the routine because 9 is less than or equal to the square root of 85.
  - C: (50,7) satisfies the routine because 7 is less than or equal to the square root of 50.
  - D: (1,1) satisfies the routine because the first number is 1 and the second number is also 1.
  - E: (1,0) does not satisfy the routine because the second number must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number, which is 1. Therefore, the only possible value for the second number is 1, not 0.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The second number (y) must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number (x).
  A: The square root of 99 is approximately 9.95, which is greater than 10. Therefore, (99,10) does not satisfy the routine.
  B: The square root of 85 is approximately 9.22, which is greater than 9. Therefore, (85,9) does not satisfy the routine.
  C: The square root of 50 is approximately 7.07, which is equal to 7. Therefore, (50,7) satisfies the routine.
  D: The square root of 1 is 1, which is equal to the second number. Therefore, (1,1) satisfies the routine.
  E: The square root of 1 is 1, which is equal to the second number. Therefore, (1,0) satisfies the routine.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are 100 employees in the company. 
Then, 75 employees take a winter vacation, and 25 employees do not take a winter vacation. 
Out of the 75 employees who take a winter vacation, 40 also take a summer vacation. So, 35 employees take only a winter vacation. 
20 employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, so 80 employees take at least one vacation. 
Therefore, 100 - 80 = 20 employees take no vacation. 
Let's represent the number of employees who take only a summer vacation as "x". 
Then, the number of employees who take a summer vacation is 40 - x (since 40 employees take a winter and a summer vacation, and x of them take only a summer vacation). 
So, the total number of employees who take a summer vacation is x + (40 - x) = 40. 
Thus, Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is (x/100)*100 = x percent. 
We can set up the following equation based on the information given: 
25 + x = 100 - 20 
Simplifying, we get: 
x = 55 
Therefore, Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is 55%. 
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Let's assume that the total number of employees in the company is 100. 

Knowledge:
- 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation.
- 40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, which means 40 employees take both vacations.
- 20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means 20 employees take neither vacation.
- We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

To find the number of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we can subtract the number of employees who take both vacations from the number of employees who take only a summer vacation. 

The number of employees who take only a summer vacation is:
75% - 40% = 35%
35% of 100 employees is 35 employees.

The answer is 35 employees, which is 35% of the total number of employees.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Let's assume that there are 100 employees in the company. 

Knowledge: 
- 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation.
- 40% of the employees take a winter and a summer vacation, which means 40 employees take both winter and summer vacation.
- 20% of the employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means 20 employees take no vacation at all.
- We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

To find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we need to subtract the number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations from the number of employees who take only a summer vacation.

The number of employees who take only a summer vacation can be found by subtracting the number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations from the number of employees who take a summer vacation:

Number of employees who take only a summer vacation = Number of employees who take a summer vacation - Number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations

Number of employees who take only a summer vacation = (100-Q)% - 40%

We know that 20% of the employees take no vacation at all, so the percentage of employees who take at least one vacation is:

100% - 20% = 80%

We also know that 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, and 40% take both winter and summer vacations. This means that the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation is:

80% - 75% = 5% + 40% = 45%

Now we can find the percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation:

Number of employees who take only a summer vacation = (100-Q)% - 40%
Number of employees who take only a summer vacation = 45% - 75%
Number of employees who take only a summer vacation = -30%

Since we cannot have a negative percentage, we can conclude that none of the answer choices are correct.

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that there are 100 employees in the company.
  75% of the employees take a winter vacation, which means 75 employees take a winter vacation.
  40% of the employees take both winter and summer vacations, which means 40 employees take both vacations.
  20% of the employees take neither winter nor summer vacations, which means 20 employees take neither vacation.
  We want to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let's assume that Q% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  The total number of employees who take a summer vacation is S = Q + 40.
  The total number of employees who take a winter vacation is W = 75.
  The total number of employees who take neither vacation is N = 20.
  The total number of employees in the company is T = 100.
  We can use these equations to solve for Q.

Calculation:
  The number of employees who take both winter and summer vacations is S ∩ W = S + W - T = Q + 40 + 75 - 100 = Q + 15.
  The number of employees who take at least one vacation is S ∪ W = S + W - S ∩ W = Q + 40 + 75 - (Q + 15) = Q + 100.
  The percentage of employees who take at least one vacation is (Q + 100) / T * 100%.
  The percentage of employees who take neither vacation is N / T * 100% = 20%.
  Therefore, the percentage of employees who take at least one vacation but not both is:
  (Q + 100) / T * 100% - N / T * 100% = (Q + 100 - 20) / T * 100% = (Q + 80) / T * 100%.

  We know that (Q + 100) / T * 100% = 100% - 20% = 80%.
  Therefore, (Q + 80) / T * 100% = (80 + 80) / 100% * T - (Q + 100) / T * 100% = 60%.
  So, Q + 80 = 60.
  Therefore, Q = -20.
  Since Q cannot be negative, the answer is none of the above.

X = Total employees who take only a summer vacation - Employees who take both vacations
X = (80 - 35) - 40
X = 5

So, 5% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A rectangular solid has 8 vertices.
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the radius of the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem. 
  
  The Pythagorean theorem states that in a right triangle, the square of the length of the hypotenuse (the longest side) is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides.
  
  In this case, the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is the hypotenuse of a right triangle with legs of length 3 and 4 and hypotenuse of length 15. 
  
  Using the Pythagorean theorem, we can find the length of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid, which is also the diameter of the sphere.
  
  A: 13.3542 is not the correct answer.
  B: 15.8113 is the correct answer.
  C: 18.3451 is not the correct answer.
  D: 19.5667 is not the correct answer.
  E: 20.8888 is not the correct answer.
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the length of its radius.
  The longest diagonal of a rectangular solid is the diagonal that joins opposite vertices of the solid.
  The length of the longest diagonal of a rectangular solid with sides of length a, b, and c is given by the formula: sqrt(a^2 + b^2 + c^2)
  In this case, a = 3, b = 4, and c = 15.

Action: 
  Calculate the length of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid:
  diagonal = sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250) = 5sqrt(10)
  
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2 x 5sqrt(10) = 10sqrt(10).
  
  Round to the nearest ten-thousandth:
  Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius of the sphere.
  A rectangular solid with dimensions 3 x 4 x 15 has a longest diagonal of length sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is also the diameter of the sphere.
Action: Answer("B")  
To see why, we can calculate the diameter of the sphere as follows:
  diameter = 2 * radius
  The radius of the sphere is equal to half of the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid.
  longest diagonal = sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250)
  radius = longest diagonal / 2 = sqrt(250) / 2
  diameter = 2 * radius = 2 * (sqrt(250) / 2) = sqrt(250) = 15.8113 (rounded to four decimal places)
Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is approximately 15.8113. Answer("B").

  Therefore, the radius of the sphere is 5*sqrt(10)/2 = (5/2)*sqrt(10).
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius, so it is 5*sqrt(10).

  The radius of the sphere is the distance from the center of the sphere to any point on the sphere.
  The distance between two opposite vertices of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  The distance between two opposite vertices of the rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem.
  The Pythagorean theorem states that for a right triangle with legs of length a and b and hypotenuse of length c, a^2 + b^2 = c^2.
  
Action: 
  The distance between two opposite vertices of the rectangular solid can be found as follows:
  d^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2
  d^2 = 9 + 16 + 225
  d^2 = 250
  d = sqrt(250) = 5*sqrt(10)
  The diameter of the sphere is twice the radius of the sphere, which is the distance between two opposite vertices of the rectangular solid.
  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 2*d = 2*5*sqrt(10) = 10*sqrt(10).

  The Pythagorean theorem states that for a right triangle with legs of length a and b and hypotenuse of length c, a^2 + b^2 = c^2.
  The rectangular solid has dimensions 3 x 4 x 15.
  The longest diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the longest diagonal of the rectangular solid.

  - Each helper can make 35 small cakes/hr, so in 3 hours, they can make 1050 small cakes.
  - Therefore, in 3 hours, each helper can make a total of 6 + 1050 = 1056 cakes.

Question: A bookshelf contains 45 books, 30 of which are hardcover and 20 of which are fiction. What is the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction?

  D: 20
  E: 30

  We are looking for the maximum number of books that are in both sets.
  We cannot have more books in both sets than the number of books in the smaller set.
Action: Answer("20")  
Explanation: 
  The maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is the smaller number of the two sets, which is 20. 
  This is because we cannot have more books in both sets than the number of books in the smaller set. 
  Therefore, the correct answer is D: 20.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can use the formula: Total = Group1 + Group2 - Both + Neither
  Total represents the total number of books on the shelf.
  Group1 represents the number of hardcover books.
  Group2 represents the number of fiction books.
  Both represents the number of books that are both hardcover and fiction.
  Neither represents the number of books that are neither hardcover nor fiction.
  
Given:
  Group1 = 30
  Group2 = 20
  Total = 45

Action: 
  We can use the formula above to solve for Both:
  Both = Group1 + Group2 - Total
  Both = 30 + 20 - 45
  Both = 5
  
  Therefore, the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is 5.
  Answer("A")

  where Both represents the number of items that belong to both Group1 and Group2.
  We are given:
  Group1 = 30 (hardcover books)
  Group2 = 20 (fiction books)
  Total = 45 (books in total)
Action: 
  Total = Group1 + Group2 - Both
  45 = 30 + 20 - Both
  Both = 5
  Therefore, the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is 5.
  Answer("A")

  B: 22
  C: 20
  D: 23
  E: 24

  We can set up a proportion: 14/10 = h/x
  We can solve for h: h = 14x/10 = 7x/5

Action:

  Answer("A")

Topic: Math
Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit?
Choices:
  A: 1,879
  B: 1,875
  C: 1,876
  D: 1,872
  E: 1,800
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cost price of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200/-.
  The profit percentage is 20%.
  The discount percentage is 20%.
  
Calculation:
  Let the marked price be x.
  Selling price after discount = 0.8x
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  Profit percentage = (Profit/Cost price) * 100
  Given that, Profit percentage = 20%
              Discount percentage = 20%
  => Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  => 0.8x = 1.2 * 1200
  => x = 1800/0.8
  => x = 2250
  Therefore, the marked price should be Rs. 2250/-
  Answer: Option E) 1,800.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  Profit percentage = (Profit / Cost price) * 100
  Discounted price = Selling price - (Discount percentage / 100) * Selling price
  
Let's assume that the selling price is x.
Given that the cost price is Rs. 1200, and Karan wants to make a 20% profit, the selling price can be calculated as follows:
  Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  x = 1200 + (20/100) * 1200
  x = 1200 + 240
  x = 1440
  
Now, Karan wants to offer a 20% discount on the selling price, which means the discounted price can be calculated as follows:
  Discounted price = Selling price - (Discount percentage / 100) * Selling price
  Discounted price = 1440 - (20/100) * 1440
  Discounted price = 1440 - 288
  Discounted price = 1152
  
Therefore, Karan should mark the sewing machine at Rs. 1,875 to make a 20% profit after offering a 20% discount.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price be M.
  Profit % = 20%
  Cost price = Rs. 1200/-
  Discount % = 20%
  Selling price = Marked price - Discount
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  Profit % = (Profit / Cost price) * 100
  We need to find the marked price.
  
Solution:
  Let's first calculate the selling price.
  Selling price = Marked price - Discount
  Profit = Selling price - Cost price
  Profit % = (Profit / Cost price) * 100
  We know that the profit percentage is 20%.
  Therefore, (Profit / Cost price) * 100 = 20%
  Profit = (20/100) * 1200 = Rs. 240/-
  Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  Selling price = 1200 + 240 = Rs. 1440/-
  We know that the discount percentage is 20%.
  Therefore, Discount = (20/100) * Marked price
  Marked price - Discount = Selling price
  Marked price - (20/100) * Marked price = 1440
  Marked price * (1 - 20/100) = 1440
  Marked price * (80/100) = 1440
  Marked price = 1440 * (100/80) = Rs. 1800/-
  Therefore, Karan should mark the sewing machine at Rs. 1800/-.
  
Action: Answer("E")

  Therefore, the marked price should be Rs. 1800.

Question: John would make the 3-letter codes with diffenrent 5 vowels and 20 consonants with the condition that the middle letter must be vowel and the first letter and the third letter must be different from each other and are both consonant. How many different codes can be made?
Choices:
  A: 1,980
  B: 2,020
  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We have 5 vowels and 20 consonants.
  The middle letter must be vowel.
  The first and third letters must be different from each other and are both consonant.
  We need to find the number of different 3-letter codes that can be made.
  
Solution:
  We can choose the first letter in 20 ways (since there are 20 consonants).
  We can choose the third letter in 19 ways (since it must be different from the first letter and there are 19 consonants left).
  We can choose the middle letter in 5 ways (since there are 5 vowels).
  Therefore, the total number of different codes that can be made is 20 x 5 x 19 = 1,900.
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  There are 5 vowels and 20 consonants.
  The middle letter must be vowel.
  The first and third letters must be different from each other and are both consonant.
  We have 20 choices for the first and third letters.
  We have 5 choices for the middle letter.
  After choosing the first and third letters, we have 19 choices for the second letter and 4 choices for the last letter.
  The number of ways to choose 2 letters out of 20 is 20C2 = 190.
  The number of ways to choose 1 letter out of 5 is 5C1 = 5.
Action: Answer("C")  
To calculate the number of different codes, we multiply the number of choices for each position: 20 * 5 * 19 * 5 * 4 = 38,000. However, we have counted each code twice (once with the first letter as the "first letter" and once with the third letter as the "first letter"), so we need to divide by 2 to get the final answer: 38,000 / 2 = 19,000.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 11 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's say the number of staplers produced on Monday is x.
  10% of the staplers produced on Monday were defective. Therefore, the number of defective staplers produced on Monday is 0.1x.
  90% of the staplers produced on Monday were non-defective. Therefore, the number of non-defective staplers produced on Monday is 0.9x.
  2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. Therefore, the number of non-defective staplers rejected is 0.02 times 0.9x, which is 0.018x.
  We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected, so we can set up an equation: 0.018x = 72.
  Solving for x, we get x = 4000.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let N be the total number of staplers produced on Monday.

  The number of non-defective staplers that were rejected by mistake is 2% of the non-defective staplers, which is 0.02(0.9N) = 0.018N.
  We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected, so 0.018N = 72.
  Solving for N, we get N = 4000.

  We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected, so 0.018x = 72.
  Solving for x, we get x = 4000.

  Then, we have the equation: MX = D
  After 3 men drop out, the equation becomes: (M-3)(X+Y) = D, where Y is the additional amount each man has to contribute.
  We need to find the value of Y.
  We can simplify the equation as follows: MX - 3X + MY - 3Y = D
  Since MX = D, we can substitute it in the equation: D - 3X + MY - 3Y = D
  Simplifying further, we get: Y = 3X/(M-3)

  So, the total amount contributed by M men is MD/M = D.
  After 3 men drop out, there are M-3 men left.

  Therefore, each man has to contribute (D/(M-3)) - (D/M) = (DM - D(M-3))/(M(M-3)) = 3D/(M(M-3))

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 15 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - If two events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities. That is, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  - The probability that at least one of two events A or B occurs is equal to the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring. That is, P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  
Solution:
  Let P(B) be the probability that event B occurs.
  We know that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.
  Using the formula for P(A or B), we have:
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))  [since A and B are independent, P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) = 0.6 * P(B)]
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)
  0.4P(B) = 0.36
  P(B) = 0.9
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both A and B occurring is equal to the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  - The probability that at least one of two events A or B occurs is equal to the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  
Action: 
  Let's use the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) to find the probability of event B occurring:
  - P(A or B) = 0.96
  - P(A) = 0.6
  - P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) (since A and B are independent)
  - We can substitute these values into the formula and solve for P(B):
      0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))
      0.36 = 0.4 * P(B)
      P(B) = 0.9
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9, which corresponds to choice E. Answer("E").

Response 6:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both A and B occurring is the product of the probabilities of each event occurring: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is the sum of the probabilities of each event occurring minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We can use the formula P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) to find the probability of event B occurring.
  
Solution:
  Let P(B) = x.
  P(A) = 0.6.
  P(A or B) = 0.96.
  P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) = 0.6x.
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B) = 0.6 + x - 0.6x = 0.4 + 0.4x.
  0.4 + 0.4x = 0.96.
  0.4x = 0.56.
  x = 0.56/0.4 = 1.4/1 = 7/5 = 1.4.
  Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 1.4.
  However, the probability of an event cannot be greater than 1.
  Therefore, the answer is not one of the choices.
  None of the above.
Response 7:
Knowledge:
  If events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of two events occurring is equal to the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both events occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  We are given P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.

Solution:
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B) - 0.6P(B)
  0.96 - 0.6 = -0.2P(B)
  0.36 = -0.2P(B)
  P(B) = -0.36 / -0.2
  P(B) = 1.8 / 10
  P(B) = 0.18

Question: Two balls A and B rotate along a circular track. Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes. Ball B makes 5 full rotation in 35 minutes. If they start rotating now from the same point, when will they be at the same starting point again?
Choices:
  A: 1 hour and 31 minutes
  B: 2 hour and 31 minutes
  C: 3 hour and 31 minutes
  D: 4 hour and 31 minutes
  E: 5 hour and 31 minutes
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The number of rotations made by a ball is directly proportional to the time taken to make the rotations.
  If two balls start at the same point and rotate around a circular track, they will be at the same starting point again when they have made the same number of rotations.
  Ball A makes 2 rotations in 26 minutes, so it makes 1 rotation in 13 minutes.
  Ball B makes 5 rotations in 35 minutes, so it makes 1 rotation in 7 minutes.
  The two balls will be at the same starting point again when they have made the same number of rotations.
  The least common multiple of 13 and 7 is 91.
  Ball A will make 7 rotations in 91 minutes.
  Ball B will make 13 rotations in 91 minutes.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The number of rotations of a ball is proportional to the time it rotates.
  - The two balls will meet again when they complete an equal number of rotations.
  - We can find the least common multiple (LCM) of the number of rotations of each ball to determine when they will meet again.

Solution:
  - Ball A makes 2 rotations in 26 minutes, so its rate is 2/26 rotations per minute, or 1/13 rotations per minute.
  - Ball B makes 5 rotations in 35 minutes, so its rate is 5/35 rotations per minute, or 1/7 rotations per minute.
  - The LCM of 13 and 7 is 91, so the balls will meet again after 91 rotations.
  - Ball A will complete 91 rotations in (91 rotations) / (1/13 rotations per minute) = 1183 minutes.
  - Ball B will complete 91 rotations in (91 rotations) / (1/7 rotations per minute) = 637 minutes.
  - The balls will meet again after the same amount of time has passed for both, which is the LCM of 1183 and 637.
  - The LCM of 1183 and 637 is 167,591 minutes, or approximately 2 days, 8 hours, and 31 minutes.

Topic: Math
Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If two objects are similar, then the ratio of their corresponding sides is the same.
  In this case, the ratio of the height of the flagstaff to the length of its shadow is the same as the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow.
  Let x be the height of the building.
  Then, we have the proportion: 17.5/40.25 = x/28.75
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.5
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If two objects are similar, their corresponding sides are proportional.
  The ratio of the height of the flagstaff to its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of the building to its shadow.

Let x be the height of the building.
Then we can set up the proportion:
17.5 / 40.25 = x / 28.75

To solve for x, we can cross-multiply and simplify:
17.5 * 28.75 = 40.25 * x
x = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25
x = 12.5

x = 12.5

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let a and b be the highest and lowest scores, respectively.
  The average of a and b is (a + b)/2.
  The average score for the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students.
  The sum of all scores is (z * y).
  We need to exclude the highest and lowest scorers, so we need to subtract (a + b) from the sum of all scores.
  The number of students whose scores we are averaging is (z - 2), since we are excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  
Calculation:
  The average of the highest and lowest score is x, so we have:
  (a + b)/2 = x
  a + b = 2x
  
  The average score for the entire class is y, so we have:
  (sum of all scores)/z = y
  sum of all scores = z * y
  
  We need to exclude the highest and lowest scorers, so we have:
  (sum of all scores - a - b)/(z - 2) = average score excluding highest and lowest
  
  Substituting (a + b) with 2x and simplifying, we get:
  ((z * y) - 2x)/(z - 2) = average score excluding highest and lowest
  
  Therefore, the answer is (D) (zy – 2x)/(z -2). 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let H be the highest score and L be the lowest score.
  The average of H and L is (H + L)/2.
  The average score for the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students.
  The sum of all scores is H + L + sum of all other scores.
  There are z - 2 students who are not the highest or lowest scorers.
  The sum of all other scores is y * (z - 2).
  The average score for the entire class is y = (H + L + y * (z - 2))/z = (H + L)/z + (y * (z - 2))/z.
  The average of the highest score and the lowest score is (H + L)/2 = x.
  Therefore, H + L = 2x.

  The average score for the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students, which is y = (H1 + H2 + ... + Hz)/z, where H1, H2, ..., Hz are the scores of each student.
  We need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, which is the sum of all scores excluding H and L divided by the number of students excluding 2, which is (H2 + H3 + ... + Hz-1)/(z-2).
Action: Answer("D")  
To find the answer, we need to express H and L in terms of x, y, and z. Since the average of H and L is x, we have (H+L)/2 = x, which means H+L = 2x. We also know that y = (H1 + H2 + ... + Hz)/z, which means Hz = yz. Therefore, we can express H and L in terms of x, y, and z as follows:
H = (yz + 2x - 2)/(2)
L = (yz - 2x + 2)/(2)
Now we can find the sum of all scores excluding H and L as follows:
(H2 + H3 + ... + Hz-1) = (H1 + H2 + ... + Hz) - H - L = yz - (yz + 2x - 2)/(2) - (yz - 2x + 2)/(2) = zy - 2x
Therefore, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is (zy - 2x)/(z-2), which is answer choice D.

  D: 58

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 22 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An astronaut weighing 211 pounds on Earth would weigh 182 pounds on Venus. The weight of the astronaut on Venus would be approximately what percent of the astronaut’s weight on Earth?
Choices:
  A: 50%
  B: 60%
  C: 70%
  D: 86%
  E: 90%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The weight of an object on a planet is proportional to the planet's gravitational force acting on the object.
  The gravitational force acting on an object is proportional to the planet's mass and inversely proportional to the square of the planet's radius.
  Venus has a mass of approximately 0.815 Earth masses and a radius of approximately 0.949 Earth radii.
  To calculate the percent of weight on Venus compared to Earth, we can use the formula: (Weight on Venus / Weight on Earth) * 100%.
Action: 
  First, we need to calculate the weight of the astronaut on Venus:
  Weight on Venus = (Weight on Earth / Earth's gravitational force) * Venus's gravitational force
  Weight on Venus = (211 / 9.807) * (0.815 * 9.807 / 0.949^2)
  Weight on Venus ≈ 182
  Now we can calculate the percent of weight on Venus compared to Earth:
  Percent of weight on Venus = (Weight on Venus / Weight on Earth) * 100%
  Percent of weight on Venus = (182 / 211) * 100%
  Percent of weight on Venus ≈ 86%
  Answer: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Weight on Venus = 182 pounds
  Weight on Earth = 211 pounds
  We need to find the percentage of the weight on Earth that the astronaut weighs on Venus.
  The formula to calculate percentage is: (part/whole) x 100
  
Calculation:
  Percentage = (182/211) x 100
  Percentage = 0.8625 x 100
  Percentage = 86.25

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The weight of an object on a planet is proportional to the planet's mass and the object's mass, but inversely proportional to the square of the planet's radius. Venus has a mass of 0.815 Earth masses and a radius of 0.949 Earth radii.
  To find the percent, we can use the formula: percent = (part/whole) x 100

Action: 
  First, we can calculate the weight of the astronaut on Venus using the proportion: 
  weight on Venus = (weight on Earth x mass of Venus) / (mass of Earth)
  weight on Venus = (211 x 0.815) / 1 = 171.965
  Next, we can calculate the percent of the astronaut's weight on Earth that the weight on Venus represents:
  percent = (weight on Venus / weight on Earth) x 100
  percent = (171.965 / 211) x 100
  percent ≈ 81.5
  The closest answer choice is D: 86%. 
  Therefore, Action: Answer("D")

  The shuttle travels 700m in 40 seconds, so its speed is 700/40 = 17.5 m/s
  The shuttle takes 5 seconds to pass a point, so the distance it covers during this time is 17.5 x 5 = 87.5 m
  The length of the shuttle is equal to the sum of the distances it covers during the 40 seconds and the 5 seconds.

Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is given by length times width.
  Let L be the length of the yard and W be the width of the yard.
  Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced.
  This means that the perimeter of the yard is equal to the sum of the lengths of the three fenced sides plus 10 meters.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by 2 times the sum of its length and width.
  
Solution:
  Let's use algebra to solve for L and W.
  From the problem, we know that L*W = 240.
  We also know that 2L + W + 10 = 3L + W, since the perimeter of the yard is equal to the sum of the lengths of the three fenced sides plus 10 meters.
  Simplifying this equation, we get L = 10.
  Substituting this value of L into the equation L*W = 240, we get W = 24.
  The amount of fencing needed is the sum of the lengths of the three fenced sides, which is 2L + 2W = 2(10) + 2(24) = 68 meters.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is given by length times width.
  If Alice puts up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard, then the length of the fencing needed is equal to the perimeter of the rectangle minus the length of the unfenced side.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by 2 times the length plus 2 times the width.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular yard is L and the width is W.
  We know that the area of the yard is 240 square meters, so we have:
  L x W = 240
  
  We also know that one side of the yard is 10 meters unfenced, so we have:
  L + W + L = perimeter - 10
  
  Simplifying the perimeter equation, we get:
  perimeter = 2L + 2W = L + W + L + 10 = 2L + W + 10
  
  Substituting the area equation into the perimeter equation, we get:
  2L + W + 10 = 2 x (240/W) + W + 10
  
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  2L + W = 2 x (240/W)
  2LW + W^2 = 480
  W^2 + 2LW - 480 = 0
  
  Using the quadratic formula, we get:
  W = 16 or W = -30
  
  Since the width cannot be negative, we have:
  W = 16
  L = 240/16 = 15
  
  Finally, we can calculate the length of fencing needed as:
  perimeter - 10 = 2L + W + 10 - 10 = 2 x 15 + 16 = 46

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 25 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls by the end of the day.
  - The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls.
  - The store sold all of its white golf balls.
  - The store had 600 golf balls in stock at the beginning of the day.
  
Let's assume that the store had y yellow golf balls and w white golf balls at the beginning of the day. Since the store sold all of its white golf balls, it means that the number of white golf balls sold is w. Since the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, it means that the number of yellow golf balls sold is also w. Therefore, the total number of golf balls sold is 2w. 

The store sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls, which means that it sold 0.8*600 = 480 golf balls. Therefore, we can write the equation: 

2w = 480

Solving for w, we get:

w = 240

This means that the store had 240 white golf balls and 240 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day. Therefore, the answer is 240+240 = 480.

  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54

So, x = 94.5.
Hence, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs.94.5.

Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  At each feeding session, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining food, which means the remaining food is reduced to 2/3 of its original amount.
  The dog ate 4 times (from 8:00 am to 11:00 am) before it started eating at noon.
  To calculate the percentage of the original food remaining, we need to calculate (2/3) ^ 4, which is approximately 0.2 or 20%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The dog eats once an hour, starting at 8:00 am and ending at 12:00 pm, so it eats for a total of 4 hours.
  At each feeding session, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining food, so the remaining food is reduced by 2/3 after each feeding session.
  If x is the original amount of food, then the amount of food remaining after 4 feeding sessions is (1/3)^4 * x = x/81.
  The percentage of the original food remaining is (x/81) / x * 100% = 1.23%.
  Therefore, none of the answer choices are correct.

After the first feeding session, there is 2/3 of the food remaining in the bowl, which is (2/3)F1.
After the second feeding session, there is (2/3) * (2/3) = 4/9 of the food remaining in the bowl, which is (4/9)F1.
After the third feeding session, there is (2/3) * (4/9) = 8/27 of the food remaining in the bowl, which is (8/27)F1.
After the fourth feeding session, there is (2/3) * (8/27) = 16/81 of the food remaining in the bowl, which is (16/81)F1.

Therefore, approximately 40% of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day, which is (16/81)F1 / F1 * 100% = 19.75% ≈ 20%.

Response 9:
Knowledge:

  At each feeding session, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining food in the bowl.
  We are asked to find the approximate percentage of the original food that was in the bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon.

Solution:
  Let's assume that the original amount of dog food in the bowl was 100 units.
  At the first feeding session (9:00 am), the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 100 units, which is 1/3 x 100 = 33.33 units.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl after the first feeding session was 100 - 33.33 = 66.67 units.
  At the second feeding session (10:00 am), the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 66.67 units, which is 1/3 x 66.67 = 22.22 units.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl after the second feeding session was 66.67 - 22.22 = 44.45 units.
  At the third feeding session (11:00 am), the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 44.45 units, which is 1/3 x 44.45 = 14.82 units.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl after the third feeding session was 44.45 - 14.82 = 29.63 units.
  At the fourth feeding session (noon), the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining 29.63 units, which is 1/3 x 29.63 = 9.88 units.
  Therefore, the amount of food remaining in the bowl after the fourth feeding session was 29.63 - 9.88 = 19.75 units.
  The percentage of the original food remaining in the bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon is (19.75 / 100) x 100% = 19.75%.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 28 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%.
  Let the original price of each article be x.
  After the price decrease, the new price of each article is 0.85x.
  Anna can buy 5 more articles, so she is buying a total of (5 + original number of articles) articles.
  The total cost of the articles is $300.
  We can set up the equation: 
  (original number of articles)(x) + (5)(0.85x) = $300
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  (original number of articles)(x) = $255
  The new price of each article is (total cost of original articles)/(original number of articles + 5).
  Substituting the values we have, we get:
  (255)/(original number of articles + 5) = 0.85x
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = (255)/(0.85(original number of articles + 5))
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If the price of each article decreases by 15%, then the new price is 85% of the original price.
  Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300, so the original price of each article is $300/(5+5) = $30.

Action: 
  The new price of each article is 85% of $30.
  New price = 0.85 * $30 = $25.5
  Anna can buy 5 more articles with the remaining $300, so the new selling price of each article is ($300/5) + $25.5 = $60 + $25.5 = $85.5
  Answer: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  If the price of an article decreased by x%, then the new selling price is (100-x)% of the original selling price.
  Anna was able to buy 5 more articles for $300, which means that the price of each article decreased by $60 ($300/5).
  Let the original selling price of each article be y.
  The new selling price of each article is (100-15)% of y, which is 85% of y.
  Anna can now buy each article for (85/100)*y = 0.85y.
  Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, so 5*0.85y = $300.
  Solving for y, we get y = $70.
  Therefore, the new selling price of each article is 85% of $70, which is $59.5.

Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the wholesale cost of the appliance is x.
  The original retail price of the appliance is 60% more than its wholesale cost, which means the original retail price is 1.6x.
  The appliance was actually sold for 20% less than the original retail price, which means it was sold for 0.8(1.6x) = 1.28x.
  We need to find the percentage increase from the wholesale cost to the selling price.
Action: Answer("B")  
To find the percentage increase, we can use the following formula:
  Percentage increase = (new value - old value) / old value * 100%
  Percentage increase = (1.28x - x) / x * 100%
  Percentage increase = 0.28x / x * 100%
  Percentage increase = 28%
Therefore, the appliance was sold for 28% more than its wholesale cost. The answer is (B).

  The percent increase from the wholesale cost to the selling price is (1.28W - W)/W * 100% = 28%.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 32 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular sheet is 'l' and the breadth is 'b'.
  When folded along the length, the perimeter of each part is 48cm, so the length of each part is 24cm. Therefore, the new length is l/2 and the new breadth is b. So, the perimeter of the new rectangle is 2(l/2 + b) = l + 2b = 48. 
  When folded along the breadth, the perimeter of each part is 66cm, so the breadth of each part is 33cm. Therefore, the new length is l and the new breadth is b/2. So, the perimeter of the new rectangle is 2(l + b/2) = l + b = 66.
  We have two equations: l + 2b = 48 and l + b = 66. We can solve these equations to find the values of l and b, and then we can calculate the area of the sheet.
Calculation:
  From the second equation, we get l = 66 - b.
  Substituting this value of l in the first equation, we get (66 - b) + 2b = 48.
  Solving this equation, we get b = 18 and l = 48 - 2b = 12.
  Therefore, the area of the sheet is l x b = 12 x 18 = 216 sq.cm.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded in half, the perimeter of each part is equal to the sum of the lengths of the two shorter sides plus twice the length of the crease.
  The area of a rectangle is equal to the product of its length and width.
  
Action: 
Let the length of the rectangle be L and the width be W.
When folded along the length, we get two rectangles of length L/2 and width W.
Perimeter of each part = 2(L/2 + W) = L + 2W = 48
When folded along the width, we get two rectangles of length L and width W/2.
Perimeter of each part = 2(L + W/2) = 2L + W = 66
Solving these two equations simultaneously, we get L = 22 and W = 13
Area of the rectangle = L x W = 22 x 13 = 286
Action: Answer("None of the above") 
The correct answer is not among the choices given. The area of the sheet is 286, which is not equal to any of the answer choices.

  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2(l + w), where l is the length and w is the width.
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = lw.
  
Action: 
  Let l be the length of the rectangle and w be the width.
  The perimeter of each part when folded along the length is 66cm, so we have:
  2(l/2 + w) = 66
  l + 2w = 66
  l = 66 - 2w
  
  The perimeter of each part when folded along the width is 48cm, so we have:
  2(l + w/2) = 48
  2l + w = 48
  2(66 - 2w) + w = 48
  132 - 3w = 48
  w = 28
  
  Substituting w = 28 into the equation l = 66 - 2w, we get l = 10.
  
  Therefore, the area of the rectangle is A = lw = 10 x 28 = 280.
  
  Since the rectangle is folded into two equal halves, the area of each part is 280/2 = 140.
  
  Answer: Answer("E")

  => l+w = 48
  When folded along the width, the perimeter of each part = 66cm
  Therefore, 2(l/2+w) = 66
  => l+2w = 66
  By solving the above two equations, we can find the values of l and w.
  Area of the sheet = l*w
Action: Answer("D")  1320

Knowledge:
  When a rectangular sheet is folded along one set of sides, the length of each part becomes half of the original length, while the width remains the same.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2(l + w), where P is the perimeter, l is the length, and w is the width.
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = lw, where A is the area, l is the length, and w is the width.

Let x be the length of the rectangular sheet and y be the width.
When folded along the length, each part has a perimeter of 48cm, so we have:
2(x/2 + y) = 48
x + 2y = 48

When folded along the width, each part has a perimeter of 66cm, so we have:
2(x + y/2) = 66
x + y = 33

Solving the system of equations, we get x = 18 and y = 15.

The area of the sheet is A = lw = (18)(15) = 270.

Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles

  If Bill's average speed is 15 mph, then he can travel 0.25 miles per minute.
  On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so his speed is 11 mph.
Action: 
  The distance Bill can travel on a windy day in 21 minutes is:
  distance = speed * time = (11 mph) * (21/60) hours = 3.85 miles (rounded to the nearest hundredth)
  Answer: Answer("D")

Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  If the bag contains 120 green sweets, we can use this ratio to find the number of red sweets.

Action: 
  Let's first find the number of green sweets for every 1 red sweet.
  For every 4 green sweets, there are 3 red sweets.
  So for 120 green sweets, we have (3/4) * 120 = 90 red sweets.
  Answer: Answer("A")

Knowledge:

  Solving for x, we get x = 90.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A number of friends decided to go on a picnic and planned to spend Rs. 96 on eatables. Four of them, however, did not turn up. As a consequence, the remaining ones had to contribute Rs. 4 extra, each. The number of those who attended the picnic was
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 12
  C: 16
  D: 24
  E: 25
Response 0:
Let the total number of friends be x. 
Then, the amount contributed by each person if all x friends attended the picnic would be 96/x. 
Since 4 friends did not turn up, the amount contributed by each person increased by 4. 
So, the new amount contributed by each person is (96/x) + 4. 
This means that the total amount collected after the 4 friends did not turn up is (96/x + 4) * (x-4). 
We know that this amount is equal to the original amount of Rs. 96. 
Therefore, we can form the equation: 
(96/x + 4) * (x-4) = 96
Expanding this equation, we get: 
96 - 16 + 384/x - 4x = 96
Simplifying this equation, we get: 
384/x = 4x - 80
384 = x(4x - 80)
96 = x(x - 20)
We can see that x = 24 satisfies this equation. 
Therefore, the total number of friends who attended the picnic is 24.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:

We can set up an equation based on this information:

(96/x) = ((96/x) + 4)(x-4)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

96 = (96 + 4x - 384)

Solving for x, we get:

x = 24

Therefore, the number of those who attended the picnic was 24.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 40 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which
Choices:
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  D: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y) implies [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y]
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y) is the negation of A.
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y) implies [x] + [y] + [x + y] < [2x] + [2y]
  D: L(x,y) > R(x,y) is the negation of C.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
  
Analysis:
  Since [x] and [y] are both less than or equal to x and y, respectively, then [x] + [y] ≤ x + y.
  Also, [x + y] ≤ [2x + 2y] = [2(x + y)].
  Therefore, L(x,y) ≤ [x] + [y] + [x + y] ≤ [2(x + y)] + [x] + [y] = R(x,y) + [x] + [y].
  This means that L(x,y) can never be equal to R(x,y), since L(x,y) is always less than or equal to R(x,y).

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]
  We need to find whether it is possible to find two positive real numbers x and y for which L(x,y) = R(x,y), L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y), L(x,y) < R(x,y), or L(x,y) > R(x,y).
  
Analysis:
  Let's consider each option:
  A: L(x,y) = R(x,y)
     [x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y]
     The left-hand side is at most 3x, while the right-hand side is at least 2x.
     Therefore, it is impossible for L(x,y) to be equal to R(x,y).
  B: L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)
     This is true based on the analysis of option A.
  C: L(x,y) < R(x,y)
     [x] + [y] + [x + y] < [2x] + [2y]
     [x + y] < [2x] + [2y] - [x] - [y]
     {x + y} < {2x} + {2y}
     where {a} denotes the fractional part of a.
     But {2x} and {2y} are both less than 1, so {2x} + {2y} is less than 2.
     Therefore, it is possible for L(x,y) to be less than R(x,y).
  D: L(x,y) > R(x,y)
     This cannot be true because of the analysis of option A.
     
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x.
  L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]
  R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume the marked price of the watch is M.
  The shopkeeper gave a discount of 5%, so the selling price of the watch is 0.95M.
  The shopkeeper gave a discount of 7%, so the selling price of the watch is 0.93M.
  The difference in profit is Rs. 15.
  
Calculation:
  Let's assume the cost price of the watch is C.
  Profit = M - C
  Selling price with 5% discount = 0.95M
  Profit with 5% discount = 0.95M - C
  Selling price with 7% discount = 0.93M
  Profit with 7% discount = 0.93M - C
  Profit with 5% discount - Profit with 7% discount = Rs. 15
  (0.95M - C) - (0.93M - C) = 15
  0.02M = 15
  M = 750

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the marked price of the watch is 'x'.
  The shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, which means the selling price of the watch is 95% of the marked price.
  If he gives a discount of 7%, the selling price of the watch is 93% of the marked price.
  If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit.
  So, we can form the following equation: 0.93x - (0.95x - 15) = 15
  Solving the equation, we get x = 750.

Action: Answer("D")

  We can use the formula: Selling Price = Marked Price - Discount
  We can also use the formula: Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  
Calculation:
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, the selling price becomes:
  S1 = M - 0.05M = 0.95M
  Let's assume the cost price of the watch is "C".
  So, the profit becomes:
  P1 = S1 - C = 0.95M - C

  S2 = M - 0.07M = 0.93M
  So, the profit becomes:
  P2 = S2 - C = 0.93M - C
  We know that P2 = P1 - 15
  So, 0.93M - C = 0.95M - C - 15
  Solving this equation, we get M = 750

Knowledge:
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  Let the cost price of the watch be C.
  Let the profit earned by the shopkeeper when he gives a discount of 5% be P1.
  Let the profit earned by the shopkeeper when he gives a discount of 7% be P2.
  We know that M = C + P1.
  We also know that M*(1-5%) = C + P2, and M*(1-7%) = C + (P2+15).
  We can use these equations to solve for M.
  
Calculation:
  From the given information, we can write:
  M*(1-5%) = C + P2
  M*(1-7%) = C + (P2+15)
  
  Substituting M = C + P1 in the first equation, we get:
  (C + P1)*(0.95) = C + P2
  P1 - 0.05P1 = P2 - C*0.05
  
  Substituting M = C + P1 in the second equation, we get:
  (C + P1)*(0.93) = C + P2 + 15
  P1 - 0.07P1 = P2 - C*0.07 - 15
  
  Subtracting the first equation from the second, we get:
  0.02P1 = C*0.02 + 15
  P1 = (C*0.02 + 15)/0.02
  
  Substituting this value of P1 in the first equation, we get:
  M = C + P1 = C + (C*0.02 + 15)/0.02 = 50C/49
  
  Therefore, the marked price of the watch is M = 50C/49.

Question: I have a money pouch containing Rs. 700. There are equal number of 25 paise coins, 50 paise coins and one rupee coins.
How many of each are there?
Choices:
  A: 453
  B: 651
  C: 400
  D: 487
  E: 286
Response 0:
Let's solve the problem step by step:
Let's assume that there are 'x' coins of each denomination.
The total value of 25 paise coins = 0.25x
The total value of 50 paise coins = 0.50x
The total value of one rupee coins = 1x = x
The sum of the total values of all the coins = 0.25x + 0.50x + x = 1.75x
According to the problem, the total value of all the coins is Rs. 700.
So, we can write the equation as 1.75x = 700
Solving for 'x', we get x = 400
Therefore, there are 400 coins of each denomination.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  1. Semi-perimeter = (Perimeter of the room) / 2
  2. Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y.
  3. The cost of papering the walls of the room = Cost of paper required for the walls of the room.
  4. The area of the walls of the room = (Perimeter of the room) x (Height of the room)
  5. The area of the doors and windows = 15 sq.m
  6. The cost of paper required for the walls of the room = (Area of the walls of the room) x (Cost of paper per square meter)
  7. The perimeter of the room = (2 x Height of the room) + (2 x Semi-perimeter)
  
Calculation:
  1. Let's assume the height of the room is 2x. Therefore, the semi-perimeter of the room is 5y.
  2. We know that the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. So, we can write the equation as 2x:5y.
  3. We can assume any value of x and find the value of y. Let's assume x = 1. Therefore, 2x = 2 and 5y = 5y.
  4. We can write the equation as 2:5 = 2x:5y. Substituting the values, we get 2:5 = 2:5. Therefore, the assumption is correct.
  5. Now, we can find the value of y. 2x = 2, so x = 1. Therefore, 5y = 5. So, y = 1.
  6. The perimeter of the room = (2 x Height of the room) + (2 x Semi-perimeter) = 2(2x) + 2(5y) = 4x + 10y = 4(1) + 10(1) = 14m.
  7. The area of the walls of the room = (Perimeter of the room) x (Height of the room) = 14 x 2 = 28 sq.m.
  8. The area of the doors and windows = 15 sq.m.
  9. The area of the walls to be papered = (Area of the walls of the room) - (Area of the doors and windows) = 28 - 15 = 13 sq.m.
  10. The cost of paper required for the walls of the room = (Area of the walls to be papered) x (Cost of paper per square meter) = 13 x 2 = Rs.26.
  11. Let the length of the room be L and the breadth of the room be B. Then, the height of the room is (Area of the walls of the room) / (Perimeter of the room) = (2LB) / (L + B) = 28 / 14 = 2m.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of its four walls.
  2. The cost of papering the walls of a room is equal to the product of the length of the paper, the width of the paper, and the cost per unit length of the paper.
  3. The area of a rectangular door or window is equal to the product of its length and width.
  4. The area of the walls of a room is equal to the product of the height of the room and its semi-perimeter.
  
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then we have:
  Area of walls = height x semi-perimeter = 2x x 5y = 10xy
  Length of paper required = perimeter x height = 2(2x + 5y) x 2x = 4x^2 + 20xy
  Cost of paper = length x width x cost per unit length = (4x^2 + 20xy) x 0.5 x 2 = 4x^2 + 20xy
  Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m
  Total area to be papered = Area of walls - Area of doors and windows = 10xy - 15
  
Substituting the cost and area values given in the problem, we get:
  4x^2 + 20xy = 260
  10xy - 15 = 15
  Simplifying the second equation, we get: xy = 3
  
Substituting xy = 3 in the first equation, we get:
  4x^2 + 60 = 260
  4x^2 = 200
  x^2 = 50
  x = sqrt(50) = 5sqrt(2)
  
Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 10sqrt(2).

  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  2. The cost of papering the walls of a room is equal to the product of the perimeter of the room and the cost per unit length of the paper.
  3. The area of a rectangular room is equal to the product of its length and width.
  4. The area of a door or window can be subtracted from the area of the walls to get the actual area to be papered.
  
Solution:
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then, the length of the room is 5y-4x and the width is y-2x.
The perimeter of the room is 2(5y-4x)+2(y-2x)=12y-10x.
The actual area to be papered is (12y-10x)(2x)=20x(3y-2x).
The cost of papering the walls is (20x(3y-2x)+15)(0.5)=10x(3y-2x)+7.5.
Given that the cost is Rs.260, we have 10x(3y-2x)+7.5=260. Solving for y/x, we get 3y-2x=26.
Substituting y/x=3/2, we get 9x-2x=26, which gives x=2.
Therefore, the height of the room is 2x=4 meters.

  Area of walls = 10xy - 15
  Cost of wallpapering = x * (10xy - 15)

  lb = 15/4

Let the height of the room be h. Then we have:
  h * 4y = lb
  h * 4y = 15/4
  h * 4h = 15
  h^2 = 15/4
  h = sqrt(15)/2

To solve the problem, we can use the following steps:
- Let h be the height of the room, and let s be the semi-perimeter of the room.
- We know that h:s = 2:5, so we can write h = (2/5)s.
- Let p be the perimeter of the room. Then we have s = p/2, so p = 2s.
- Let w be the width of the room. Then we have w = 50 cm = 0.5 m.
- The area of the walls is (h + w)p, and the area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m. So the area of the walls that need to be papered is (h + w)p - 15.
- The cost of papering the walls is the area of the walls that need to be papered multiplied by the cost per unit area, which is Rs.2 per sq.m. So the cost is 2[(h + w)p - 15].
- We can substitute h = (2/5)s and p = 2s into the expression for the cost to get:
  Cost = 2[(2/5)s + 0.5)(2s) - 15]
       = 2(0.4s + 1)(2s) - 15
       = 1.6s^2 + 4.4s - 15
- We can solve for s by setting the cost equal to Rs.260 and solving the resulting quadratic equation:
  1.6s^2 + 4.4s - 15 = 260
  1.6s^2 + 4.4s - 275 = 0
  s^2 + 2.75s - 171.875 = 0
  Using the quadratic formula, we get s = 10.625 or s = -12.875. Since s must be positive, we take s = 10.625.
- Finally, we can use h = (2/5)s to find the height of the room:
  h = (2/5)(10.625) = 4
Therefore, the height of the room is 4m. Answer: Answer("C")

  2x/5y = 2/5
  x = y

  x = 4.857

Solution:

The perimeter of the room is 2 x semi-perimeter = 10x.
So, the length of the room is (10x - 4x)/2 = 3x.

Given that the cost of papering the walls is Rs.260.
So, 160x^2 - 120 = 260.
Solving for x, we get x = 1.5.
Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 3m.

Choices:

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers.
  We have (x + y)^2 = x^2 + y^2 + 2xy
  We have x^2 - y^2 = 256000
  We have x + y = 1000
  We can use the equations above to solve for x and y.
  
Solution:
  We have (x + y)^2 = x^2 + y^2 + 2xy
  Substituting x^2 - y^2 = 256000, we get (x + y)^2 = 256000 + 2xy + (x^2 + y^2)
  Substituting x + y = 1000, we get 1000^2 = 256000 + 2xy + 2(x^2 - y^2)
  Substituting x^2 - y^2 = 256000, we get 1000^2 = 256000 + 2xy + 2(256000)
  Simplifying the equation above, we get xy = 372000
  We have x + y = 1000
  We have x - y = sqrt(x^2 - y^2) = sqrt(256000) = 160 * sqrt(5)
  Solving the system of equations above, we get x = 500 + 80 * sqrt(5) and y = 500 - 80 * sqrt(5)
  Therefore, the answer is not one of the given choices.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume the two numbers are x and y. We know that x^2 - y^2 = 256000 and x + y = 1000.
  We can factor x^2 - y^2 as (x+y)(x-y), so we have (x+y)(x-y) = 256000.
  We also know that x+y = 1000, so we can substitute that into the equation to get (1000)(x-y) = 256000.
  Solving for x-y gives us x-y = 256.
  We now have two equations with two variables, which we can solve to find x and y.

Action: 
  We can use the equation x+y = 1000 and x-y = 256 to solve for x and y.
  Adding the two equations gives us 2x = 1256, so x = 628.
  Substituting that into x+y = 1000 gives us y = 372.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Let's first calculate the yearly production cost: 
420 units/month x $110/unit x 12 months/year = $554,400/year

To make a profit of at least $626,400, the yearly revenue from sales must be:
$554,400/year + $626,400/year = $1,180,800/year

The yearly revenue from sales is the selling price per component multiplied by the number of components sold in a year. Since the company sells 420 units every month, the number of components sold in a year is:
420 units/month x 12 months/year = 5,040 units/year

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400 is:
$1,180,800/year ÷ 5,040 units/year = $234/unit

Choices:
A: 226
B: 230
C: 240
D: 260
E: 280

Action: Answer("C")

Knowledge:

Calculation:
  The yearly production cost is 420 x 12 x $110 = $554,400.
  To make a profit of $626,400, the yearly revenue should be $1,180,800.
  The revenue from selling 420 units of the component is 420 x selling price per unit.
  Therefore, selling price per unit should be at least $1,180,800 / 420 = $280.

5,040p - 554,400 ≥ 626,400 

5,040p ≥ 1,180,800 

p ≥ 234.127 

The minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400 is $234.127, which is closest to option B.

Yearly profit = Yearly revenue - Yearly production costs

We know that the yearly profit must be at least $626,400, so we can set up the following inequality:

Yearly revenue - Yearly production costs ≥ $626,400

5040 x selling price per unit ≥ 1180800

selling price per unit ≥ 234.2857

Rounding up to the nearest whole number, we get:

selling price per unit ≥ 235

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit will be at least $626,400 is $235.

Question: A sales person gets a 10% commission on each sale he makes. How many sales of $250 each must he make in order to reach a salary of at least $1000?

  A: 15
  B: 24
  C: 25
  D: 40

  The sales person wants to make at least $1000.
  Each sale is $250.
  
Plan:

  The commission on each sale is 10% of $250, which is $25.
  The total amount the sales person earns from the x sales is 25x.
  We want to find the value of x that makes 25x at least $1000.
  So we can write the inequality 25x >= 1000.
  Solving for x, we get x >= 40.

Action: Answer("D")

  If the sales person makes a sale of $250, he gets a commission of 10% of $250 = $25.

  To calculate the commission, we multiply the sale amount by the commission rate (10% or 0.1).
  The total salary earned will be the sum of the base salary and the commission earned from sales.
  
Solution:

  The total salary must be at least $1000, so we can write the equation:
  x + 0.1(250n) >= 1000
  where n is the number of sales needed to reach the salary of $1000.
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  x + 25n >= 100
  Subtracting x from both sides, we get:
  25n >= 100 - x
  Dividing both sides by 25, we get:
  n >= (100 - x)/25
  Since n must be a whole number, we can round up the result of (100 - x)/25 to the nearest integer.
  If the sales person makes 15 sales, the commission earned will be 0.1(250)(15) = $375, and the total salary will be $x + $375.
  If the sales person makes 16 sales, the commission earned will be 0.1(250)(16) = $400, and the total salary will be $x + $400.
  Therefore, the sales person must make at least 16 sales to reach a salary of at least $1000.

Action:

  Then, A travels 5 km towards east, which means A is now 5 km east and 3 km south from the starting point, forming a right-angled triangle with the starting point.
  Next, A travels 3 km towards north, which means A is now 3 km north, 5 km east, and 3 km south from the starting point, forming a right-angled triangle with the starting point.
  Finally, A travels 2 km towards west, which means A is now 2 km west, 3 km north, 5 km east, and 3 km south from the starting point, forming a right-angled triangle with the starting point.
  We can now calculate the distance between A and the starting point using Pythagoras Theorem.
  The distance between A and the starting point = square root of (3^2 + 5^2 + 3^2 + 2^2) = square root of 47.

           = square root of (9 + 25)
           = square root of 34

         ≈ 5.83 km - 2 km
         ≈ 3.83 km
         ≈ 4 km (rounded to the nearest km)

Topic: Math
Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let's first calculate the profits of A and B, and then we can calculate the time when C joined the business.

A invested for the whole year, so his profit share for the year will be (12/12) = 1/1 of the total profit.
B joined after 2 months, so his profit share for the year will be (10/12) = 5/6 of the total profit.
C joined after some more time, so his profit share for the year will be (x/12) of the total profit.

Now, we can write the equation for C's profit share:
C's profit share = Total profit * (x/12) * (1/3) = Rs.150,000

Solving for x, we get:
x = (150000 * 12 * 3) / (375000) = 12 months

C joined after A and B had already been in business for 12 months, so the total time when B was in business before C joined was:
Total time = 12 months - 2 months = 10 months

Therefore, the answer is:
Action: Answer("B")  i.e. 4 months.
Response 1:
Let's start by finding the ratio of profit sharing between A, B, and C. 
A's investment = Rs.40,000 for 12 months = Rs.480,000
B's investment = Rs.60,000 for 10 months = Rs.600,000
C's investment = Rs.120,000 for (12-x) months = Rs.120,000(12-x)
Total investment = Rs.1,200,000

Now, we can find the ratio of profit sharing as follows:
A : B : C = 480000 : 600000 : 120000(12-x) = 8 : 10 : 2(12-x) = 4 : 5 : 12-x

We know that C's share is Rs.150,000, which is 2/5 of the total profit. Therefore, the total profit is Rs.375,000.
Let P be the profit that C earned before he joined the business.
(4+5+12-x)P = 375000
21P = 375000
P = Rs.17,857.14

C's share of Rs.150,000 includes the profit he earned before he joined the business, which is equal to 12-x months of profit sharing.
So, we can write:
12-x = 150000/17857.14
12-x = 8.4
x = 3.6

Therefore, C joined the business 3.6 months after B joined.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales.
  We need to find the monthly sales that will make the monthly salary reach $1500.

Solution:
  Let x be the monthly sales.
  The monthly salary is S = 500 + 0.05x.
  We need to solve the equation 500 + 0.05x = 1500 for x.
  Subtracting 500 from both sides, we get 0.05x = 1000.
  Dividing both sides by 0.05, we get x = 20000.

Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The sum of k consecutive integers can be calculated as k times the average of the integers.
  If the least integer is -50, then the next integer is -49, and so on.
  The sum of k consecutive integers starting from -50 can be expressed as -50 + (-49) + ... + (last integer) = k * (average of the integers)
  The average of k consecutive integers starting from -50 can be expressed as (-50 + last integer)/2.
  We are given that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  Therefore, we can write the equation: -50 + (-49) + ... + (last integer) = k * ((-50 + last integer)/2) = 51.
  Simplifying this equation, we get: k * (last integer - 50 + last integer)/2 = 51.
  Further simplifying, we get: k * (2 * last integer - 50)/2 = 51.
  We know that the least integer is -50, so the next integer is -49, and so on.
  Therefore, the last integer is -50 + (k-1) = -51 + k.
  Substituting this value in the equation, we get: k * (2 * (-51 + k) - 50)/2 = 51.
  Simplifying this equation, we get: k^2 - 51k + 52 = 0.
  Factoring this quadratic equation, we get: (k-1)(k-51) = 0.
  Therefore, k = 1 or k = 51.
  We are given that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51, so k cannot be 1.

Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The rate of the liquid is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - We want to find how many minutes it will take y gallons to pass through the drain.
  - There are 60 seconds in 1 minute.
  
Solution:
  - Let's first find the rate of the liquid in gallons per minute:
    - w/25 gallons every x seconds = (w/25) * (60/x) gallons per minute = 12w/5x gallons per minute
  - The time it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain is:
    - y gallons / (12w/5x) gallons per minute = (5xy)/(12w) minutes
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Rate = Volume / Time
  The liquid passes through the drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  We need to find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain.
  We can use the formula: Time = Volume / Rate
  
Calculations:
  The rate of the liquid = w/25 gallons every x seconds
  Therefore, the rate of the liquid in gallons per minute = (w/25) * 60/x = 12w/x
  
  Time = Volume / Rate
  Time = y / (12w/x) = yx / (12w)
  Time in minutes = (yx / (12w)) / 60 = yx / (720w)
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - The rate of the liquid passing through the drain is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - We want to find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain.
  - We can use the formula: time = amount / rate
Action: Answer("A") 

Using the formula: time = amount / rate, we can find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain as:

time = y / (w/25 * x) = 25xy / w

Converting this time to minutes, we get:

time in minutes = (25xy / w) * (1 minute / 60 seconds) = 5xy / (12w)

Therefore, the answer is (A) y/(1200xy).

time = y gallons / (w/25 * x gallons/seconds)
time = y * 25 * x / w seconds
time = (y * 25 * x / w) / 60 minutes
time = 5xy / (12w) minutes

  - We want to find how many minutes it will take y gallons to pass through the drain.

  - In one minute, the liquid passes through (w/25) * x * 60 gallons.
  - To find how many minutes it will take y gallons to pass through the drain, we can set up the equation: (w/25) * x * 60 * t = y, where t is the time in minutes.
  - Solving for t, we get t = y / (1200wx).
  - Therefore, the answer is A: y/(1200xy).
